_Thought for 50s_

I found a genuinely stronger theorem. It sharpens the overlap lane a lot.

The key observation is that under the branch-independent 2D closure law, the “translated replication” branch is not merely local at a witness. It **globalizes** on the entire connected overlap interval. Once you combine that with the corrected endpoint regimes, three of the four overlap subcases become much cleaner.

---

## 1. Globalization of the translated branch under 2D closure

Assume we are in the open overlap regime
\[
B_0+B_2>B_1,
\]
with overlap interval
\[
I_q=(q_-,q_+)=\Omega_0\cap\Omega_2.
\]
Let
\[
\phi_0,\phi_2:I_q\to \mathbf R_u
\]
be the outer inverse branches, and define
\[
W(q):=\phi_2'(q)-\phi_0'(q)
=
\frac1{\widehat Q'(\phi_2(q))}-\frac1{\widehat Q'(\phi_0(q))}.
\]

Assume the branch-independent 2D closure law
\[
\Xi'(u)=H\!\left(\widehat Q(u),\frac1{\widehat Q'(u)},\Xi(u)\right)
\]
on the two outer runs, so the branchwise reciprocal-slope pairs
\[
Y_i(q):=\left(\frac1{\widehat Q'(\phi_i(q))},\ -\Xi(\phi_i(q))\right)
\]
solve the same first-order ODE in \(q\).

Now suppose at some point \(q_*\in I_q\) we are in the translated branch:
\[
\phi_2(q)-\phi_0(q)\equiv C
\qquad\text{near }q_*.
\]
Then in particular
\[
W(q)\equiv 0
\qquad\text{near }q_*,
\]
so
\[
\frac1{\widehat Q'(\phi_2(q))}=\frac1{\widehat Q'(\phi_0(q))}
\quad\text{and}\quad
\Xi(\phi_2(q))=\Xi(\phi_0(q))
\]
near \(q_*\). Thus
\[
Y_2(q)=Y_0(q)
\qquad\text{near }q_*.
\]

But \(Y_0\) and \(Y_2\) satisfy the same first-order ODE on the connected interval \(I_q\). By uniqueness and continuation,

\[
\boxed{
Y_2(q)\equiv Y_0(q)\quad\text{on the whole overlap interval }I_q.
}
\]

Hence
\[
W(q)\equiv 0\quad\text{on }I_q,
\]
and therefore
\[
\phi_2(q)-\phi_0(q)\equiv C
\quad\text{on }I_q.
\]

So we get:

### Global translated-branch theorem
Under branch-independent 2D closure, if translated replication holds at one point of the overlap interval, then it holds on the entire connected overlap interval.

That is already a real strengthening.

---

## 2. Immediate consequences by overlap regime

Now combine this with the corrected endpoint asymptotics.

### CC overlap
Here
\[
q_-=d_2,\qquad q_+=d_1,
\]
and
\[
W(q)\to +\infty\quad(q\downarrow q_-),
\qquad
W(q)\to -\infty\quad(q\uparrow q_+).
\]
So \(W\equiv0\) on \(I_q\) is impossible.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{In CC overlap, the translated branch is impossible under 2D closure.}
}
\]

Since earlier we proved every zero of \(W\) is either translated replication or a strict downward crossing, it follows that in CC:

\[
\boxed{
\text{there is exactly one nontranslation same-value / same-slope witness.}
}
\]

This is now a genuine theorem-shaped conclusion.

### CR overlap
Here
\[
q_-=d_2,\qquad q_+=d_3,
\]
and
\[
W(q)\to +\infty\quad(q\downarrow q_-).
\]
So again \(W\equiv0\) on \(I_q\) is impossible.

Hence:

\[
\boxed{
\text{In CR overlap, the translated branch is impossible under 2D closure.}
}
\]

So CR witness existence reduces purely to the endpoint sign at \(q_+\):
- if \(W(q_+^-)<0\), there is exactly one witness;
- if \(W(q_+^-)\ge 0\), there is no witness.

Equivalently, in CR:

\[
\boxed{
\text{there is a witness } \Longleftrightarrow
\widehat Q'(u_{0,3})>\widehat Q'(u_3),
}
\]
and if it exists, it is unique.

### RC overlap
Symmetrically, translated replication is impossible because
\[
W(q)\to -\infty\quad(q\uparrow q_+),
\]
so \(W\equiv0\) is impossible. Hence:

\[
\boxed{
\text{In RC overlap, the translated branch is impossible under 2D closure.}
}
\]

And witness existence is equivalent to the left endpoint sign:
\[
\boxed{
\text{there is a witness } \Longleftrightarrow
\widehat Q'(u_0)>\widehat Q'(u_{2,0}),
}
\]
and if it exists, it is unique.

### RR overlap
This is the only overlap regime where translated replication is not killed immediately by endpoint blow-up, because both endpoint limits of \(W\) are finite.

So RR remains the only exceptional overlap case where the translated branch could in principle survive.

This is a big simplification:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Under 2D closure, translated replication is impossible in CC/CR/RC and can survive only in RR.}
}
\]

---

## 3. The overlap lane now collapses almost completely outside RR

So the corrected overlap transport picture under 2D closure is now:

- **CC:** exactly one witness, always;
- **CR:** zero or one witness, determined by the right endpoint slope comparison;
- **RC:** zero or one witness, determined by the left endpoint slope comparison;
- **RR:** only exceptional case needing separate interior analysis.

That is much stronger than before. It means that on three of the four overlap subcases, there is no local ambiguity left at all once 2D closure is granted.

In particular, the whole “translated replication vs nontranslation witness” fork is now only a real issue in RR.

---

## 4. A sharpened theorem statement

The previous one-crossing theorem can now be strengthened to the following.

### Overlap rigidity theorem under 2D closure
Assume branch-independent 2D closure on the outer runs.

Then on any open overlap interval \(I_q\):

1. every zero of \(W=\Delta'\) is either
   - a point on the global translated branch \(W\equiv0\), or
   - a strict downward crossing;

2. in the CC, CR, and RC overlap regimes, the global translated branch is impossible;

3. therefore:
   - CC has exactly one witness;
   - CR has at most one witness, and it exists iff \(W(q_+^-)<0\);
   - RC has at most one witness, and it exists iff \(W(q_-^+)>0\);
   - RR is the only remaining exceptional overlap case.

This is, I think, the cleanest conditional theorem on this lane so far.

---

## 5. A useful new consequence for the local \(K\)-picture

Earlier we showed that every nontranslation witness under 2D closure satisfies
\[
K(q_*)>0.
\]
Now, in CC/CR/RC, translated replication is impossible. So in those regimes:

\[
\boxed{
\text{every witness is nontranslation, hence every witness satisfies }K(q_*)>0.
}
\]

So the witness is automatically a strict local maximum of \(\Delta\), with no competing translated branch to worry about.

This means the curvature-defect sign at the witness is now a **theorem** in CC/CR/RC under 2D closure, not just a fork statement.

---

## 6. Best next attack from here

The sharpened strategic picture is now very clear.

### Main live target outside RR
Prove the CR/RC endpoint slope comparison:
\[
\widehat Q'(u_{0,3})>\widehat Q'(u_3)
\quad\text{or}\quad
\widehat Q'(u_0)>\widehat Q'(u_{2,0}).
\]
If either comparison is proved, the corresponding witness exists and is unique.

So the whole non-RR overlap lane is now reduced to:
- prove 2D closure,
- prove these endpoint slope inequalities.

### Main live target in RR
RR is now the only regime where translated replication can still survive. So RR should be attacked separately by trying to rule out
\[
W\equiv0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\phi_2(q)-\phi_0(q)\equiv C
\]
on the entire overlap interval.

That makes RR genuinely exceptional and worth isolating.

---

## 7. Bottom line

The strongest new gain is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Under 2D closure, translated replication globalizes on the overlap interval.}
}
\]

From that:

\[
\boxed{
\text{In CC, CR, and RC overlap, translated replication is impossible.}
}
\]

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{CC has exactly one witness;}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{CR/RC have zero or one witness, determined solely by endpoint slope comparison;}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{RR is the only remaining exceptional overlap regime.}
}
\]

That is the sharpest and cleanest reduction I have obtained on the corrected overlap transport lane.

## Assistant (2026-04-22 02:03:00)

_Thought for 1m 4s_

I found a real no-go, and it sharpens the attack a lot.

The right conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{outside the CC subcase, witness existence is \emph{not} forced by the quotient-visible overlap geometry alone.}
}
\]

So in CR/RC/RR, the same-value / same-slope witness problem cannot be closed from the amplitude list or window overlap data by themselves. One needs extra source-side or transport-closure input.

That is a useful negative result, because it tells us exactly where pure \(\Delta/\Xi\)-geometry hits a ceiling.

## 1. Why this matters

After the sign correction, the open overlap regime is
\[
B_0+B_2>B_1,
\]
and the witness problem is about zeros of
\[
W(q):=\Delta'(q)
=
\frac{1}{\widehat Q'(\phi_2(q))}
-
\frac{1}{\widehat Q'(\phi_0(q))}
=
p_2(q)-p_0(q)
\]
on the overlap interval \(I_q\).

In CC, endpoint blow-up forces
\[
W(q)\to +\infty \text{ at the left end},\qquad
W(q)\to -\infty \text{ at the right end},
\]
so a witness is automatic.

But in CR/RC/RR, at least one overlap endpoint is regular, so one or both endpoint limits of \(W\) are finite. The question is then whether the endpoint sign forces a zero.

What I can now show is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{for CR/RC/RR, the existence or nonexistence of a witness is not determined by the walk/amplitude data alone.}
}
\]

That is the core negative finding.

## 2. Abstract inverse-branch model

On a monotone run, the inverse branch \(\phi(q)\) is determined by its reciprocal slope
\[
p(q):=\phi'(q)=\frac{1}{\widehat Q'(\phi(q))}>0.
\]
Conversely, any positive analytic \(p(q)\) on a value interval gives a monotone inverse branch by integration:
\[
\phi(q)=\phi(q_0)+\int_{q_0}^q p(s)\,ds.
\]

So, at the quotient-visible level, the overlap transport problem is controlled by choosing two positive analytic reciprocal-slope profiles \(p_0,p_2\) on the common overlap interval, subject only to the endpoint blow-up/finite behavior dictated by the regime.

The overlap amplitude data \((B_0,B_1,B_2)\) determine the value interval \(I_q\), but they do **not** determine these reciprocal-slope profiles.

That is the source of the nonuniqueness.

## 3. Explicit CR countermodels

Take the overlap interval
\[
I_q=(0,1),
\]
and consider the CR endpoint pattern:
- left overlap endpoint critical on the right outer run,
- right overlap endpoint regular on both runs.

Choose
\[
p_2(q)=1+q^{-1/2},
\]
so \(p_2(q)\to+\infty\) as \(q\downarrow 0\), and \(p_2(1)=2\).

Now choose two different left reciprocal-slope profiles.

### Model A: witness exists
Let
\[
p_0^{(A)}(q)\equiv 3.
\]
Then
\[
W_A(q)=p_2(q)-p_0^{(A)}(q)=q^{-1/2}-2.
\]
So
\[
W_A(q)\to+\infty \quad (q\downarrow 0),
\qquad
W_A(1)=-1<0.
\]
Hence \(W_A\) has a zero in \((0,1)\), so there is a same-value / same-slope witness.

### Model B: no witness
Let
\[
p_0^{(B)}(q)\equiv \frac32.
\]
Then
\[
W_B(q)=p_2(q)-p_0^{(B)}(q)=q^{-1/2}-\frac12.
\]
So
\[
W_B(q)\to+\infty \quad (q\downarrow 0),
\qquad
W_B(1)=\frac12>0.
\]
Hence \(W_B(q)>0\) on all of \((0,1)\), so there is no witness.

Both models have the same qualitative CR overlap geometry:
- same open overlap interval,
- same endpoint type (critical left / regular right),
- same window combinatorics.

Yet one has a witness and the other does not.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{CR witness existence is not determined by overlap geometry alone.}
}
\]

## 4. RC and RR are the same

The same construction works in RC by reversing the roles of the two sides.

For RR, both endpoint limits are finite, so the nonuniqueness is even more obvious: choose two positive analytic functions \(p_0,p_2\) on \(I_q\) with whatever endpoint values you like, and \(W=p_2-p_0\) can be arranged to:
- never vanish,
- vanish once,
- or vanish multiple times,
unless one imposes additional structure such as the 2D closure law.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{RR witness behavior is maximally underdetermined at the pure overlap-geometry level.}
}
\]

## 5. Structural theorem: only CC is forced by pure overlap geometry

So the clean structural theorem is:

### Pure overlap-geometry ceiling
Within the abstract quotient-visible inverse-branch framework:

1. in CC, witness existence is forced by endpoint asymptotics;
2. in CR/RC/RR, witness existence is not forced by the overlap interval or amplitude/walk data alone.

Equivalently, only CC is automatic at the purely quotient-visible overlap-geometry level.

This is, I think, the cleanest negative result on the overlap lane so far.

## 6. What this means for the attack

This tells us exactly what extra input is needed in CR/RC/RR.

To get a witness outside CC, one must prove some additional theorem of one of these kinds:

1. **endpoint slope comparison**:
   \[
   \widehat Q'(u_{0,3})>\widehat Q'(u_3)
   \quad\text{or}\quad
   \widehat Q'(u_0)>\widehat Q'(u_{2,0});
   \]

2. **2D closure + endpoint sign control**, giving at most one witness and reducing existence to endpoint tests;

3. some direct **source-side asymmetry law** that forces the needed sign of
   \[
   W(q_+^-)\ \text{or}\ W(q_-^+).
   \]

So the attack is now much better targeted.

It says:

\[
\boxed{
\text{do not spend more time trying to force CR/RC/RR witnesses from overlap geometry alone. That is impossible.}
}
\]

Instead, the right next move is to attack the missing extra input directly.

## 7. Best next attack from here

There are now two clear live directions.

### Attack A: prove the endpoint slope comparison theorem
This is the natural next target in CR/RC:
\[
\widehat Q'(u_{0,3})>\widehat Q'(u_3)
\quad\text{(CR)},
\qquad
\widehat Q'(u_0)>\widehat Q'(u_{2,0})
\quad\text{(RC)}.
\]
That would produce the witness in those regimes.

### Attack B: prove the 2D closure law
If 2D closure
\[
\Xi'(u)=H\!\left(\widehat Q(u),\frac1{\widehat Q'(u)},\Xi(u)\right)
\]
holds, then:
- every nontranslation witness is a strict downward crossing of \(W\);
- translated replication globalizes;
- witness multiplicity collapses to at most one;
- and CR/RC/RR all reduce to endpoint sign tests for \(W\).

So 2D closure is still the strongest structural upgrade available.

## 8. Bottom line

The main new mathematical finding is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Only CC overlap forces a same-value / same-slope witness at the pure quotient-visible overlap-geometry level.}
}
\]

And more sharply:

\[
\boxed{
\text{CR/RC/RR witness existence is underdetermined by the overlap interval and amplitude/walk data alone.}
}
\]

So the overlap lane has a real ceiling:
- **CC** is automatic;
- **everything else needs extra transport/source input**.

That is the clearest no-go I’ve obtained on this part of the attack, and it tells us exactly where to focus next.

## Assistant (2026-04-22 02:05:07)

_Thought for 1m 59s_

I found a real correction and a sharper ceiling. It changes the overlap story in a useful way.

The clean statement is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{pure quotient-visible overlap geometry forces a witness only in the \emph{strict} CC subcase.}
}
\]

Once endpoint equalities are allowed, even CC can support **global translated replication**, so the earlier “CC automatically gives a unique witness” was too strong.

## 1. The real endpoint criterion

Let
\[
\Omega_0=(d_0,d_1),\qquad \Omega_2=(d_2,d_3),
\qquad
I_q=(q_-,q_+)=(\max\{d_0,d_2\},\,\min\{d_1,d_3\}).
\]
On the overlap interval define
\[
W(q)=\Delta'(q)=\frac1{\widehat Q'(\phi_2(q))}-\frac1{\widehat Q'(\phi_0(q))}.
\]

The old endpoint blow-up argument only works when **exactly one** outer branch is singular at each overlap end. That requires the strict inequalities
\[
d_2>d_0,\qquad d_1<d_3.
\]
In that case:
- at \(q_-=d_2\), only the right branch is critical, so \(W\to+\infty\);
- at \(q_+=d_1\), only the left branch is critical, so \(W\to-\infty\).

Hence a witness is forced.

So the correct automatic-witness statement is:

\[
\boxed{
d_2>d_0\ \text{and}\ d_1<d_3
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
W\text{ has a zero in }I_q.
}
\]

That is the **strict CC** subcase.

## 2. Why the old CC claim was too strong

If one of the endpoint equalities
\[
d_2=d_0
\quad\text{or}\quad
d_1=d_3
\]
holds, then both outer branches are singular at that overlap end. Their reciprocal-slope blow-ups can cancel. So endpoint asymptotics no longer force any sign of \(W\) there.

This is not just a technicality; it really happens.

### Explicit model
Take
\[
\widehat Q(u)=\sin u
\]
on the three consecutive monotone runs
\[
R_0=\left[-\frac{\pi}{2},\frac{\pi}{2}\right],\qquad
R_1=\left[\frac{\pi}{2},\frac{3\pi}{2}\right],\qquad
R_2=\left[\frac{3\pi}{2},\frac{5\pi}{2}\right].
\]
Then
\[
d_0=d_2=-1,\qquad d_1=d_3=1,
\]
so
\[
B_0=B_1=B_2=2,
\qquad
B_0+B_2>B_1.
\]
Thus we are in the overlap regime, and in fact
\[
\Omega_0=\Omega_2=(-1,1).
\]

The outer inverse branches are
\[
\phi_0(q)=\arcsin(q),\qquad
\phi_2(q)=2\pi+\arcsin(q),
\]
so
\[
\phi_2(q)-\phi_0(q)\equiv 2\pi,
\qquad
W(q)\equiv 0.
\]

So here we have:
- open overlap;
- same-value / same-slope everywhere;
- global translated replication;
- no endpoint sign forcing at all.

This proves:

\[
\boxed{
\text{CC overlap does \emph{not} by itself exclude the translated branch.}
}
\]

So the right dichotomy is not “CC vs non-CC,” but “strict CC with noncoincident endpoint values” versus everything else.

## 3. New structural ceiling

This gives a stronger no-go than before:

\[
\boxed{
\text{outside strict CC, witness existence is not forced by overlap geometry alone;}
}
\]
and more sharply,
\[
\boxed{
\text{even in CC, if }d_0=d_2\text{ and }d_1=d_3,\text{ translated replication can occur abstractly.}
}
\]

So the whole overlap lane has a harder ceiling than I was previously claiming.

Pure quotient-visible overlap data do **not** kill the translated branch. They only force a witness in strict CC.

That means the real remaining work has to use extra input:
- source-side slope comparison,
- 2D closure,
- or package-level structure strong enough to exclude translated replication.

## 4. Corrected overlap taxonomy

The overlap lane should now be organized as follows.

### Strict CC
\[
d_2>d_0,\qquad d_1<d_3.
\]
Automatic witness by endpoint asymptotics.

### Degenerate CC
One or both equalities
\[
d_2=d_0,\qquad d_1=d_3
\]
hold.
No automatic endpoint sign forcing. The translated branch is abstractly possible.

### CR / RC
Only one overlap endpoint is singular. Witness existence reduces to one explicit finite endpoint sign:
\[
W(q_+^-)
=
\frac1{\widehat Q'(u_3)}-\frac1{\widehat Q'(u_{0,3})}
\quad\text{(CR)},
\]
or
\[
W(q_-^+)
=
\frac1{\widehat Q'(u_{2,0})}-\frac1{\widehat Q'(u_0)}
\quad\text{(RC)}.
\]

### RR
Both overlap endpoints are regular. Pure overlap geometry gives no automatic witness and no automatic exclusion of the translated branch.

So the actual “easy” subcase is only strict CC.

## 5. What survives from the previous attack

The local transport fork at a **given witness** is still good:

At any point \(q_*\in I_q\) with
\[
W(q_*)=0,
\]
under branch-independent 2D closure, either:

1. translated replication holds locally,
   \[
   \phi_2(q)-\phi_0(q)\equiv C,
   \]
or
2. the witness is a strict downward crossing, equivalently
   \[
   K(q_*)>0,
   \qquad
   K(q)=\Xi(\phi_2(q))-\Xi(\phi_0(q)).
   \]

What changed is simply this: **existence of such a witness is not automatic except in strict CC**.

So the right logical order is now:

1. first get a witness;
2. then apply the local fork.

That is cleaner.

## 6. Strongest consequence for the global strategy

This means the most promising next theorem targets are now even clearer.

### Target A: exclude translated replication by extra structure
Because the overlap geometry itself does not kill it, even in degenerate CC. If you can prove
\[
\phi_2(q)-\phi_0(q)\equiv C
\]
is impossible on disjoint outer runs for RH-specific or package-level reasons, then the overlap lane simplifies dramatically.

### Target B: prove the CR/RC endpoint slope comparison
That is now the only missing step to make witnesses automatic in CR/RC:
\[
\widehat Q'(u_{0,3})>\widehat Q'(u_3)
\quad\text{or}\quad
\widehat Q'(u_0)>\widehat Q'(u_{2,0}).
\]

### Target C: prove 2D closure
Because once a witness exists, 2D closure rigidifies it immediately into:
- translated replication, or
- strict quadratic witness \(K(q_*)>0\).

So 2D closure is still the best structural upgrade.

## 7. Bottom line

The sharpest new finding is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Only the strict CC overlap subcase forces a same-value / same-slope witness by pure overlap geometry.}
}
\]

And the strongest counterexample is the equal-window translated model
\[
\widehat Q(u)=\sin u,
\]
which shows:

\[
\boxed{
\text{open overlap and even CC do not exclude global translated replication at the quotient-visible level.}
}
\]

So the overlap lane has a stricter ceiling than I had before. The real next attacks are now unambiguously:

- exclude translated replication by extra structure,
- prove CR/RC endpoint slope comparison,
- and/or prove branch-independent 2D closure.

That is the sharpest continuation of the attack I can honestly give after this correction.

## Assistant (2026-04-22 02:08:17)

I found a sharper target than “prove a witness exists everywhere.” The overlap geometry has a hard ceiling, so the best attack now is to go straight at the only branch that pure overlap doesn’t kill: **translated replication**. If that branch dies under RH-specific structure, the whole overlap lane becomes much more rigid immediately.

_Thought for 2m 46s_

I found a real structural theorem, and it sharpens the overlap lane much more than my previous endpoint-case bookkeeping.

The key new point is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{On an open outer-overlap interval, translated replication can occur only if the two outer windows are exactly equal: }
d_0=d_2,\ d_1=d_3.
}
\]

That is a genuine no-go, and it cleans up the overlap endgame a lot.

## 1. Setup

Assume open outer overlap
\[
\Omega_0\cap \Omega_2\neq\varnothing,
\qquad
\Omega_0=(d_0,d_1),\quad \Omega_2=(d_2,d_3),
\]
so
\[
I_q=(q_-,q_+)=(\max\{d_0,d_2\},\,\min\{d_1,d_3\}).
\]
Let
\[
\phi_0,\phi_2:I_q\to \mathbf R_u
\]
be the outer inverse branches, and define the gap
\[
\Delta(q):=\phi_2(q)-\phi_0(q).
\]

The translated branch is the condition
\[
\Delta(q)\equiv C
\qquad (q\in I_q),
\]
equivalently
\[
\phi_2(q)=\phi_0(q)+C.
\]

On the left transported source interval \(U_0:=\phi_0(I_q)\), this is
\[
\widehat Q(u+C)=\widehat Q(u).
\]
Differentiating,
\[
\widehat Q'(u+C)=\widehat Q'(u)
\qquad (u\in U_0).
\]

So translated replication forces equality of the first derivative along the whole transported left subinterval.

## 2. The endpoint obstruction

Now examine what happens at an overlap endpoint.

Suppose first that
\[
q_-=d_2>d_0.
\]
Then \(q_-\) is the left critical value of the right outer run \(R_2\), while on the left outer run \(R_0\) the same value \(d_2\) is attained at an **interior regular point** \(u_{0,2}\in R_0\). Under translated replication, as \(q\downarrow d_2\),
\[
\phi_0(q)\to u_{0,2},
\qquad
\phi_2(q)=\phi_0(q)+C\to u_{2,\mathrm{left}},
\]
the left endpoint of \(R_2\).

Passing to the limit in
\[
\widehat Q'(\phi_2(q))=\widehat Q'(\phi_0(q)),
\]
we obtain
\[
\widehat Q'(u_{2,\mathrm{left}})=\widehat Q'(u_{0,2}).
\]
But
\[
\widehat Q'(u_{2,\mathrm{left}})=0
\]
because \(u_{2,\mathrm{left}}\) is a critical point, while
\[
\widehat Q'(u_{0,2})\neq 0
\]
because \(u_{0,2}\) is interior regular on the monotone run \(R_0\).

Contradiction.

So translated replication is impossible whenever
\[
d_2>d_0.
\]

The symmetric argument at the upper overlap endpoint shows translated replication is impossible whenever
\[
d_1<d_3.
\]

Likewise, if instead
\[
d_0>d_2,
\]
then the lower overlap endpoint is critical on the left run and regular on the right, giving the same contradiction. Similarly for
\[
d_3<d_1.
\]

Therefore the only way translated replication can survive is if **both** overlap endpoints are shared critical values:
\[
d_0=d_2,\qquad d_1=d_3.
\]

This proves:

### Theorem (translated branch no-go except equal-window case)
If translated replication
\[
\phi_2(q)-\phi_0(q)\equiv C
\]
holds on a nontrivial open outer-overlap interval, then necessarily
\[
d_0=d_2,\qquad d_1=d_3,
\]
i.e.
\[
\Omega_0=\Omega_2.
\]

Equivalently, if the outer windows are not exactly equal, translated replication is impossible.

This is the strongest clean no-go I have on the overlap lane.

## 3. Consequences for the overlap taxonomy

This immediately simplifies the geometry.

There are only two kinds of overlap situations now.

### (A) Equal-window overlap
\[
d_0=d_2,\qquad d_1=d_3.
\]
Only here can the translated branch survive abstractly. The model
\[
\widehat Q(u)=\sin u
\]
on two translated outer runs shows this is a real possibility at the pure quotient-visible level.

### (B) Unequal-window overlap
At least one of
\[
d_0\neq d_2,\qquad d_1\neq d_3
\]
holds.
Then translated replication is impossible.

This is already a big simplification: in every unequal-window overlap case, any witness zero of
\[
W(q):=\Delta'(q)
\]
is automatically a nontranslation witness.

## 4. Corrected endpoint-sign table

Now let me rewrite the strict-inequality overlap cases correctly.

The endpoint sign of
\[
W(q)=\frac1{\widehat Q'(\phi_2(q))}-\frac1{\widehat Q'(\phi_0(q))}
\]
depends on which branch is critical at each overlap end.

There are four strict endpoint-order patterns:

1. \(d_2>d_0,\ d_1<d_3\):
   \[
   W(q)\to +\infty \text{ at }q_-,
   \qquad
   W(q)\to -\infty \text{ at }q_+.
   \]
   So there is at least one witness.

2. \(d_2>d_0,\ d_3<d_1\):
   \[
   W(q)\to +\infty \text{ at }q_-,
   \qquad
   W(q)\to +\infty \text{ at }q_+.
   \]
   No automatic witness.

3. \(d_0>d_2,\ d_1<d_3\):
   \[
   W(q)\to -\infty \text{ at }q_-,
   \qquad
   W(q)\to -\infty \text{ at }q_+.
   \]
   No automatic witness.

4. \(d_0>d_2,\ d_3<d_1\):
   \[
   W(q)\to -\infty \text{ at }q_-,
   \qquad
   W(q)\to +\infty \text{ at }q_+.
   \]
   So there is at least one witness.

So pure overlap geometry forces a witness exactly in patterns (1) and (4), and not in (2) and (3).

That is cleaner than the old CC/CR/RC/RR labels.

## 5. What survives under 2D closure

Now combine this with the branch-independent 2D closure law:
\[
\Xi'(u)=H\!\left(\widehat Q(u),\frac1{\widehat Q'(u)},\Xi(u)\right).
\]

Earlier we proved that under 2D closure, any zero of \(W\) is either:
- on the translated branch, or
- a strict simple zero.

Now translated replication is impossible in every unequal-window overlap case. Therefore in every unequal-window overlap case:

\[
\boxed{
\text{every zero of }W\text{ is simple.}
}
\]

So the overlap lane is now much cleaner:

- in the two strict sign-forcing patterns (1) and (4), there is at least one simple witness;
- in the two same-sign patterns (2) and (3), witness existence is not forced by geometry alone and needs extra input;
- the only place translated replication can survive is the equal-window case.

This is a sharp and useful reduction.

## 6. Best next attack from here

The overlap lane is now clearly split into two endgames.

### Unequal-window overlap
Translated replication is dead. So the only issue is witness existence and, once a witness exists, the local tower/\(K\) analysis.

Thus the best next targets are:
- in the sign-forcing patterns (1) and (4), use the local witness fork immediately;
- in the same-sign patterns (2) and (3), prove an extra endpoint slope comparison or transport theorem to force a witness.

### Equal-window overlap
This is the only regime where translated replication can survive. So it should now be isolated and attacked separately.

A very concrete next theorem target is:

> If \(\Omega_0=\Omega_2\) and translated replication holds, then the outer runs are literal translated copies on the whole common value interval.

That is already extremely rigid and may be incompatible with extra RH-specific or package-level structure even though it is allowed abstractly.

## 7. Bottom line

The strongest new finding is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Translated replication on an open overlap interval forces exact equality of the two outer windows: }\Omega_0=\Omega_2.
}
\]

So outside the equal-window case, translated replication is impossible.

That means the overlap lane is now much better organized:

- **equal-window overlap**: translated branch is the only real local loophole;
- **unequal-window overlap**: translated branch is gone, and the problem reduces to whether \(W\) has a simple zero.

This is the sharpest no-go I have on the corrected overlap transport side.

## Assistant (2026-04-22 02:18:14)

_Thought for 3m 25s_

Here is the next attack. I think the only genuinely live loophole left on the overlap side is now the **equal-window** case, and that case can be sharpened a lot by looking at the critical-end asymptotics.

The point is: once we proved that translated replication on an open overlap interval forces
\[
\Omega_0=\Omega_2,
\qquad\text{i.e.}\qquad
d_0=d_2,\quad d_1=d_3,
\]
the next question is no longer “can translated replication happen anywhere?” It is:

> in the equal-window case, what extra endpoint data are forced if translated replication is to survive?

That turns out to be very rigid.

---

## 1. Equal-window overlap and endpoint asymptotics

Assume
\[
d_0=d_2=:a,\qquad d_1=d_3=:b,
\]
so
\[
\Omega_0=\Omega_2=(a,b).
\]
Let the outer inverse branches be
\[
\phi_0,\phi_2:(a,b)\to \mathbf R_u,
\qquad
\widehat Q(\phi_i(q))=q.
\]
Define
\[
W(q):=\phi_2'(q)-\phi_0'(q)
=
\frac{1}{\widehat Q'(\phi_2(q))}
-
\frac{1}{\widehat Q'(\phi_0(q))}.
\]

Since both outer runs start at the same lower critical value \(a\) and end at the same upper critical value \(b\), both reciprocal slopes blow up at both ends. So unlike the strict CC case, endpoint blow-up by itself does not force a sign change in \(W\). But the **asymptotic blow-up rates and leading coefficients** do.

Let the lower endpoint orders on \(R_0,R_2\) be
\[
\alpha_0^- = 2r_0^-+1,\qquad \alpha_2^- = 2r_2^-+1,
\]
and the upper endpoint orders be
\[
\alpha_0^+ = 2r_0^+ +1,\qquad \alpha_2^+ = 2r_2^+ +1.
\]

Then near the lower endpoint \(q\downarrow a\), each inverse branch has the usual odd-root asymptotic
\[
\phi_i(q)=\ell_i^- + A_i^- (q-a)^{1/\alpha_i^-}+o\!\left((q-a)^{1/\alpha_i^-}\right),
\qquad A_i^->0,
\]
so
\[
\phi_i'(q)
=
c_i^- (q-a)^{-\beta_i^-}+o\!\left((q-a)^{-\beta_i^-}\right),
\qquad
\beta_i^-:=1-\frac{1}{\alpha_i^-},
\qquad
c_i^-=\frac{A_i^-}{\alpha_i^-}>0.
\]

Similarly near the upper endpoint \(q\uparrow b\),
\[
\phi_i'(q)
=
c_i^+ (b-q)^{-\beta_i^+}+o\!\left((b-q)^{-\beta_i^+}\right),
\qquad
\beta_i^+:=1-\frac{1}{\alpha_i^+},
\qquad
c_i^+>0.
\]

So the sign of \(W\) near each end is determined lexicographically by the pair
\[
(\beta_i^\pm, c_i^\pm).
\]

That is the key sharpening.

---

## 2. Endpoint asymptotic sign rule for \(W\)

At the lower end \(q\downarrow a\), we have
\[
W(q)=\phi_2'(q)-\phi_0'(q).
\]
Therefore:

- if \(\beta_2^->\beta_0^-\), then
  \[
  W(q)\to +\infty;
  \]
- if \(\beta_2^-<\beta_0^-\), then
  \[
  W(q)\to -\infty;
  \]
- if \(\beta_2^-=\beta_0^-\), then the sign is determined by \(c_2^- - c_0^-\).

Exactly the same holds at the upper end \(q\uparrow b\), with the upper asymptotic data \((\beta_i^+,c_i^+)\).

So the equal-window overlap case still has an endpoint sign test — it is just subtler than in strict CC. It depends on odd endpoint orders and leading inverse-root coefficients.

This gives a concrete theorem-shaped reduction:

\[
\boxed{
\text{In equal-window overlap, witness existence is controlled by the two endpoint asymptotic comparisons of }W.
}
\]

If the asymptotic sign of \(W\) is opposite at the two ends, then a witness exists by IVT.

---

## 3. Translated replication forces exact endpoint asymptotic matching

Now suppose the translated branch holds:
\[
\phi_2(q)-\phi_0(q)\equiv C
\qquad (q\in(a,b)).
\]
Then
\[
\phi_2'(q)\equiv \phi_0'(q),
\]
so
\[
W(q)\equiv 0.
\]

Therefore the lower endpoint asymptotics of \(\phi_2'\) and \(\phi_0'\) must agree exactly:
\[
\beta_2^-=\beta_0^-,
\qquad
c_2^-=c_0^-.
\]
Equivalently:
- the lower odd critical orders must match,
- and the leading inverse-branch coefficients must match.

Similarly at the upper endpoint:
\[
\beta_2^+=\beta_0^+,
\qquad
c_2^+=c_0^+.
\]

So translated replication forces exact matching of **both** endpoint asymptotic packages.

This is a very strong no-go.

### Endpoint-asymptotic no-go for translated replication
If translated replication holds on an equal-window overlap interval, then the lower and upper critical endpoint asymptotics of the two outer runs match exactly:
\[
(\alpha_0^-,A_0^-)=(\alpha_2^-,A_2^-),
\qquad
(\alpha_0^+,A_0^+)=(\alpha_2^+,A_2^+).
\]

Therefore any mismatch in odd order or leading coefficient at either end kills translated replication immediately.

That is a genuine new structural theorem.

---

## 4. Consequence: the equal-window case splits into matched and mismatched endpoints

So the equal-window case is not one monolithic exceptional regime anymore. It now splits naturally into:

### Equal-window, endpoint-mismatched
At least one of the endpoint asymptotic packages differs. Then translated replication is impossible. Moreover, if the induced asymptotic sign of \(W\) differs between the two ends, then a witness exists automatically.

### Equal-window, endpoint-matched
Both lower and upper asymptotic packages match exactly. Only here can translated replication survive.

This is the sharpest localization of the translated branch I have so far.

---

## 5. What this means under 2D closure

Now combine this with the earlier 2D closure theorem.

Under branch-independent 2D closure:
- every zero of \(W\) is either on the translated branch or is a strict downward crossing;
- the translated branch globalizes on the connected overlap interval.

So in the equal-window case:

- if endpoint asymptotics are mismatched, translated replication is impossible;
- therefore any witness is automatically a nontranslation witness;
- hence every zero of \(W\) is a strict downward crossing.

Thus in the mismatched equal-window case, witness structure becomes just as rigid as in the unequal-window case.

So the only genuinely stubborn overlap subcase left is now:

\[
\boxed{
\text{equal-window overlap with exact matching of both endpoint asymptotic packages.}
}
\]

That is a much smaller exceptional set than “equal-window overlap” as a whole.

---

## 6. A very concrete next theorem target

The next clean target is now:

### Endpoint-matching rigidity theorem
If an equal-window overlap interval has matching lower and upper endpoint asymptotic packages, then the two outer runs are locally translated copies.

If this were true, then the translated branch would not just be compatible with endpoint matching — it would be forced by it. That would classify the exceptional case completely.

Even without the full theorem, the new reduction is already very strong:

- unequal-window overlap: translated replication impossible;
- equal-window but endpoint-mismatched: translated replication impossible;
- only equal-window + endpoint-matched remains.

That is a dramatic narrowing.

---

## 7. Best next attacks

The best next moves are now very clear.

### Attack A: endpoint slope/jet comparison
Use the endpoint asymptotic data to prove that in the RH setting the two outer runs cannot match at both ends unless they are literally translated copies.

### Attack B: classify the matched equal-window case
Assume
\[
\Omega_0=\Omega_2
\]
and both endpoint asymptotic packages match. Try to prove this forces
\[
\phi_2(q)-\phi_0(q)\equiv C.
\]
That would isolate the exceptional translated branch completely.

### Attack C: continue the nontranslation overlap lane
Outside the matched equal-window case, translated replication is gone. Then under 2D closure the witness problem reduces to strict downward crossings of \(W\), and the remaining burden is just endpoint sign comparison / existence of a zero.

---

## 8. Bottom line

The strongest new finding is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Translated replication on an overlap interval forces exact matching of the endpoint asymptotic packages at both overlap ends.}
}
\]

So the translated branch survives only in the tiny subcase:

\[
\boxed{
\Omega_0=\Omega_2
\quad\text{and}\quad
\text{lower/upper endpoint asymptotics match exactly.}
}
\]

Everywhere else, translated replication is impossible.

That is the sharpest structural reduction I can now give on the overlap transport lane.

## Assistant (2026-04-22 02:20:00)

_Thought for 22s_

Here is the next attack. I think the equal-window exceptional branch can now be sharpened to a **full-run translated-copy theorem**. That is stronger than the local statements I gave before.

## 1. Setup

Assume we are in the overlap regime and on the translated branch:
\[
\phi_2(q)-\phi_0(q)\equiv C
\qquad (q\in I_q),
\]
where
\[
I_q=\Omega_0\cap\Omega_2.
\]
Equivalently, on the transported left-run interval
\[
U_0:=\phi_0(I_q)\subset R_0
\]
we have
\[
\widehat Q(u+C)=\widehat Q(u)
\qquad (u\in U_0).
\]

Earlier we showed this already forces equal windows:
\[
\Omega_0=\Omega_2,
\qquad
d_0=d_2,\quad d_1=d_3.
\]

Now I want to show something stronger:

\[
\boxed{
\text{translated replication on the overlap interval actually globalizes to the whole outer runs.}
}
\]

## 2. Globalization by analytic continuation

Define
\[
F(u):=\widehat Q(u+C)-\widehat Q(u).
\]
On any connected open set where both \(u\) and \(u+C\) stay in the analytic domain of \(\widehat Q\), \(F\) is analytic.

Since \(F\equiv 0\) on the nonempty open interval \(U_0\), the identity theorem implies:

\[
\boxed{
F(u)\equiv 0
\text{ on the entire connected component of }
\{u:\ u,\ u+C \text{ both lie in the domain}\}
\text{ containing }U_0.
}
\]

So the equality
\[
\widehat Q(u+C)=\widehat Q(u)
\]
is not just local on the overlap transport interval. It propagates as far as both the left run and its translate coexist in the analytic domain.

For our outer-run situation, the natural connected component is the whole left outer run \(R_0\), provided \(R_0+C\) stays inside the right outer run \(R_2\). That is exactly what the endpoint analysis now gives.

## 3. Endpoint propagation

Because \(\Omega_0=\Omega_2=(a,b)\), the lower and upper endpoint values match:
\[
\widehat Q(\ell_0)=\widehat Q(\ell_2)=a,
\qquad
\widehat Q(r_0)=\widehat Q(r_2)=b,
\]
where \(\ell_i,r_i\) are the left and right endpoints of the outer runs \(R_i\).

Now let \(u\downarrow \ell_0\) inside \(R_0\). Since
\[
\widehat Q(u+C)=\widehat Q(u)
\]
on \(R_0\cap(R_2-C)\), the image values on the translated side approach the same lower endpoint value \(a\). By monotonicity of \(R_2\), the only possible limit point is \(\ell_2\). So
\[
\ell_0+C=\ell_2.
\]
Similarly, taking \(u\uparrow r_0\),
\[
r_0+C=r_2.
\]

Therefore
\[
R_2=R_0+C
\]
as intervals, and the translated identity extends across the full run:

\[
\boxed{
\widehat Q(u+C)=\widehat Q(u)\qquad (u\in R_0),
}
\]
with
\[
R_2=R_0+C.
\]

So we get the stronger theorem:

### Full-run translated-copy theorem
If translated replication holds on a nontrivial open overlap interval, then the two outer windows are equal and the two outer runs are literal translates of each other:
\[
R_2=R_0+C,
\qquad
\widehat Q|_{R_2}=\widehat Q|_{R_0}\circ(\,\cdot\,-C).
\]

That is a real strengthening.

## 4. Consequences for critical endpoint germs

Once we know the full-run translated-copy theorem, all endpoint germ data match automatically:

\[
\widehat Q^{(m)}(u+C)=\widehat Q^{(m)}(u)
\qquad (u\in R_0,\ m\ge 0),
\]
hence in particular the lower and upper critical endpoint germs match exactly under translation:
- same odd order,
- same leading coefficient,
- same full Taylor germ.

So the earlier “endpoint asymptotics must match” result is now a corollary of a much stronger statement.

In other words, the translated branch is no longer just “compatible with” equal-window endpoint matching. It **is** full translated-copy symmetry of the two outer runs.

## 5. Why this is useful

This dramatically narrows the exceptional branch.

Previously the exceptional overlap branch was:

- equal windows,
- matching endpoint asymptotics,
- maybe translated replication.

Now it is simply:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the two outer runs are full translated copies.}
}
\]

That is a much more rigid and attackable object. Any RH-specific or package-level theorem that forbids two disjoint outer runs in the same three-run block from being exact translates would kill the translated branch completely.

So the overlap lane now splits into:

1. **translated-copy branch**:
   \[
   R_2=R_0+C,\qquad \widehat Q(u+C)=\widehat Q(u)\ \text{on }R_0;
   \]

2. **nontranslation branch**:
   every witness, once it exists and 2D closure holds, is a strict downward crossing of
   \[
   W=\Delta',
   \]
   with
   \[
   K(q_*)>0
   \]
   at the witness.

That is the cleanest fork yet.

## 6. A second gain: the translated-copy branch forces periodicity on the outer-shell geometry

Because
\[
\widehat Q(u+C)=\widehat Q(u)\quad\text{on }R_0,
\]
the whole reciprocal-slope tower also matches by translation:
\[
J_n(u+C)=J_n(u)\qquad (u\in R_0,\ n\ge 1).
\]
So every transported scalar on the outer runs is \(C\)-periodic across the two shells.

This means that in the translated branch there is **no residual transport defect at all** on the outer shells. The entire branch is a rigid periodic-copy phenomenon.

So if the rest of the proof can exclude exact translated-copy outer shells, then the whole overlap exceptional branch dies at once.

## 7. Best next attack from here

I think the next target is now much sharper than before.

### New top target
Prove that two disjoint outer runs in the three-run fixed-shear configuration cannot be exact translated copies:
\[
R_2=R_0+C,\qquad \widehat Q(u+C)=\widehat Q(u)\text{ on }R_0.
\]

This is no longer a vague “kill translated replication” target. It is a concrete full-run symmetry exclusion problem.

A few possible routes:
- use the middle run \(R_1\) to show a translated pair of outer runs would force an impossible repeated shell pattern;
- connect translated-copy outer shells to the updated nonmixed 4-point affine same-value/same-slope lane;
- prove a source-side uniqueness statement forbidding two distinct translates of the same monotone quotient germ inside one three-run block.

### Secondary target
If translated-copy exclusion is hard, then proceed on the nontranslation branch:
- get 2D closure,
- reduce to one-crossing of \(W\),
- and then attack endpoint slope comparison in the non-exceptional overlap subcases.

## 8. Bottom line

The strongest new finding is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Translated replication on an overlap interval globalizes: it forces the two outer runs to be full translated copies.}
}
\]

So the overlap transport lane is now reduced to a very rigid dichotomy:

\[
\boxed{
\text{either exact translated-copy outer shells,}
}
\]
or
\[
\boxed{
\text{nontranslation overlap with simple witness structure controlled by }W=\Delta'.
}
\]

That is the sharpest attack reduction I have so far on the overlap side.

## Assistant (2026-04-22 02:57:01)

_Thought for 16s_

Here is the full recap of my lane, with the things I think are genuinely worth preserving for the paper team, and with the things that should stay marked as conditional or exploratory.

At a high level, my attack started as a broad “hidden state on the exact fixed-shear lane” investigation, but it has compressed a lot. The current picture is that most plausible **local** or **finite** hidden mechanisms are dead, and the real residual burden sits on the exact fixed-shear overlap transport problem downstairs in the quotient variable, together with one very rigid translated-copy exceptional branch. That matches the recent draft updates well: the residual mixed corner is really \((S=0)\cap(K_v=0)\), the quartic–sextic rung is not the source of a live local rescue, and the honest remaining targets are transport-closure or package-level, not “one more scalar.” 

I’ll split the recap into: eliminations and ceilings, structural reductions that I think are real, the corrected overlap transport picture, the closure hierarchy I extracted, and the best remaining targets.

## 1. Big eliminations and ceilings from this attack

The first big message is negative but useful: I do not think the residual exact fixed-shear obstruction is another local field.

More specifically, my attack now strongly suggests all of the following.

There is no serious reason to keep searching for a second explicit pointwise highest-new generator on this lane. The current explicit highest-new package still looks same-tower over \(r=q^{(7)}\), and the recent draft update explicitly leans the honest remaining burden toward package/provenance-level structure, not another new local scalar. 

There is no plausible residual obstruction in a finite local symmetric two-atom invariant built from the visible exact fixed-shear package. Once repeated pairs on the exact fixed-shear slice are forced to be involutive \((t,-t)\), any finite-order local analytic involution-symmetric datum built from the visible package descends to the quotient variable \(u=t^2\). So the residual lane is not hiding in a forgotten local pair-jet scalar.

There is no plausible residual obstruction in a finite hidden chamber-label theory, unless it reduces to some visible subtree statistic. And under the natural “no exogenous birth label” assumption, even that collapses to visible count-type data. Further surgery arguments suggest those count-type data cannot matter for any boundary law that is local finite-jet analytic. So I no longer think the residual exact fixed-shear problem is a finite combinatorial hidden-memory problem.

There is no serious remaining run-local hidden profile degree of freedom on a single sign-run. On a monotone run, the quotient-visible geometry has no internal critical structure; the run is just an interval of values. So any genuinely quotient-visible run-local quantity should collapse to the value interval, hence to the amplitude
\[
B(R)=\int_R |\widehat{\mathcal D}(u)|\,du.
\]
Under even mild functorial subdivision, that should linearize. So I do not think the obstruction is hiding inside one run.

There is no plausible one-vertex hidden scalar beyond the adjacent amplitude pair \((B_-,B_+)\). Around one odd critical point, the visible two-run block is completely described by those two drops/rises and max/min orientation. So again, I do not think the residual obstruction is a one-vertex hidden datum.

That whole elimination package fits the current draft’s direction: the local collision-cancellation chart kills the naive swap-even scalar rescue, and the quartic–sextic rung is already inert for the explicit lobe-amplitude obstruction. 

## 2. Structural reductions that I think are real

The most important positive reductions I got are these.

First, the right object is the **quotient-visible chain**, not the source pair. On the exact fixed-shear slice the repeated-pair geometry is involutive and quotient-diagonal, so the real transport object is downstairs in \(u=t^2\), not the raw \((h_1,h_2)\)-pair.

Second, on a strict same-value transport interval between outer runs, the correct scalar to study is the outer-branch gap
\[
\Delta(q)=\phi_2(q)-\phi_0(q),
\]
where \(\phi_0,\phi_2\) are the two outer inverse branches of \(\widehat Q\) at the same value \(q\). That reparametrizes the residual exact fixed-shear lane as a one-variable value-transport problem, which is exactly the way the recent update now frames it. 

Third, the corresponding curvature observable
\[
\Xi(u)=\frac{\widehat Q''(u)}{(\widehat Q'(u))^3}
\]
enters with exact inverse-branch identities:
\[
\phi_i'(q)=\frac{1}{\widehat Q'(\phi_i(q))},
\qquad
\phi_i''(q)=-\Xi(\phi_i(q)).
\]
So
\[
\Delta'(q)
=
\frac{1}{\widehat Q'(\phi_2(q))}
-
\frac{1}{\widehat Q'(\phi_0(q))},
\]
and
\[
\Delta''(q)
=
\Xi(\phi_0(q))-\Xi(\phi_2(q)).
\]
This gives the explicit scalar defect
\[
K(q):=\Xi(\phi_2(q))-\Xi(\phi_0(q))=-\Delta''(q).
\]

That is the cleanest concrete residual scalar I extracted from the lane.

Fourth, the reciprocal-slope tower is the right jet language at a same-value witness:
\[
J_1(u)=\frac1{\widehat Q'(u)},
\qquad
J_{n+1}(u)=J_1(u)\partial_u J_n(u),
\]
and along inverse branches
\[
\mathcal J_{n,i}(q):=J_n(\phi_i(q)).
\]
Then
\[
\frac{d}{dq}\mathcal J_{n,i}(q)=\mathcal J_{n+1,i}(q),
\]
and
\[
\Delta^{(m)}(q)=\mathcal J_{m,2}(q)-\mathcal J_{m,0}(q).
\]
So at any same-value/same-slope witness, the first transverse defect is always a finite even mismatch in this tower, unless translated replication holds. That is a useful exact local fork.

## 3. Important corrections I found along the way

There were two corrections that matter.

The first is the three-run sign correction. The inverse-branch transport setup belongs only to the **open overlap** regime
\[
B_0+B_2>B_1,
\]
not to the separation regime
\[
B_1>B_0+B_2.
\]
So all of the \(\Delta/\Xi\) analysis is conditional on genuine outer overlap, not on strict separation. The update note explicitly corrected this, and my later attack was rebased on that correction. 

The second is the witness-sign correction. At an actual overlap witness where \(\Delta'(q_*)=0\), the witness is a local **maximum** of \(\Delta\), not a minimum. So under the natural 2D closure law I describe below, one gets
\[
\Delta''(q_*)<0
\qquad\Longleftrightarrow\qquad
K(q_*)>0.
\]
That sign is now the correct one.

## 4. The corrected overlap transport picture

After the sign correction, the overlap lane looks like this.

Open outer overlap means
\[
I_q=\Omega_0\cap\Omega_2
=
(\max\{d_0,d_2\},\,\min\{d_1,d_3\})
\neq \varnothing.
\]

On this interval define
\[
W(q):=\Delta'(q)
=
\frac{1}{\widehat Q'(\phi_2(q))}
-
\frac{1}{\widehat Q'(\phi_0(q))}.
\]
Then a same-value / same-slope witness is exactly a zero of \(W\).

The endpoint behavior of \(W\) depends on which outer branch is singular or regular at each overlap endpoint. This gives the right overlap taxonomy. In some strict endpoint-order patterns, \(W\) is forced to change sign by blow-up; in others it is not. The big ceiling I found is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{outside the strict sign-forcing subcase, witness existence is not forced by overlap geometry alone.}
}
\]

More sharply, I constructed and analyzed countermodel behavior showing that in CR/RC/RR-type overlap situations, one can have the same overlap interval and same window data, but either have a witness or not, depending on the reciprocal-slope profiles. So pure overlap geometry does not determine witness existence there.

That is an important no-go, because it means the live problem outside the easiest overlap subcase needs **extra** input:
- endpoint slope comparison,
- a closure law,
- or source/package structure.

That is now a real ceiling on the lane.

## 5. Translated replication: what survives and what does not

A major part of the attack was to isolate the translated branch:
\[
\phi_2(q)-\phi_0(q)\equiv C.
\]

I got several useful reductions here.

First, translated replication on any nontrivial open overlap interval forces equality of the outer windows:
\[
\Omega_0=\Omega_2,
\qquad
d_0=d_2,\quad d_1=d_3.
\]
So outside the equal-window case, translated replication is impossible.

Second, in the equal-window case, translated replication forces exact matching of the critical endpoint asymptotic packages at both overlap ends: same odd order, same leading inverse-branch coefficient, and in fact the same full translated endpoint germ. Any mismatch kills the translated branch immediately.

Third, and strongest: translated replication on the overlap interval actually globalizes. If
\[
\phi_2(q)-\phi_0(q)\equiv C
\]
on a nontrivial open overlap interval, then analytic continuation plus endpoint propagation force the two outer runs themselves to be full translated copies:
\[
R_2=R_0+C,
\qquad
\widehat Q(u+C)=\widehat Q(u)\quad (u\in R_0).
\]

So the translated branch is no longer just a local loophole. It is a full-run translated-copy symmetry of the two outer shells.

This is one of the strongest things to come out of the attack.

It means the overlap transport lane now has a very rigid exceptional branch:
- either exact translated-copy outer shells,
- or nontranslation transport.

That is much cleaner than the original “maybe hidden reset” language.

## 6. The branch-independent closure hierarchy

This is probably the nicest structural package I extracted.

At a same-value / same-slope witness, the reciprocal-slope tower gives a value-space jet hierarchy. If the outer-branch dynamics close in a branch-independent way at low dimension, then the tower collapses fast.

The hierarchy is:

### 1D closure
A law of the form
\[
\widehat Q''=G(\widehat Q,\widehat Q')
\]
or equivalently \(\Xi\) determined branch-independently by \((\widehat Q,1/\widehat Q')\), forces immediate collapse: at a witness, equality of the first reciprocal slope already implies translated replication.

So 1D branch-independent closure kills the nontranslation branch outright.

### 2D closure
The natural 2D closure law is
\[
\Xi'(u)=H\!\left(\widehat Q(u),\frac1{\widehat Q'(u)},\Xi(u)\right).
\]
Equivalently, the pair
\[
\left(\mathcal J_1,\mathcal J_2\right)
=
\left(\frac1{\widehat Q'(\phi(q))},\ -\Xi(\phi(q))\right)
\]
satisfies the same first-order ODE on both outer branches.

Under this 2D closure law, every nontranslation same-value / same-slope witness is already **quadratic**:
\[
K(q_*)>0
\qquad\Longleftrightarrow\qquad
\Delta''(q_*)<0.
\]
So under 2D closure, the witness is a strict local maximum of \(\Delta\). That is the quadratic witness theorem.

This is much stronger than the earlier vague “some even tower mismatch” statement.

I also got a nice general meta-theorem from the tower viewpoint: if the branch dynamics close in dimension \(m\), then the first even tower mismatch order at a nontranslation witness must satisfy \(N\le m\). So the tower is a very explicit closure detector.

## 7. Zero structure and one-crossing under 2D closure

Under the 2D closure law, the witness zeros of
\[
W(q)=\Delta'(q)
\]
simplify a lot.

At any zero of \(W\), exactly one of two things happens:
- translated replication holds locally;
- or the zero is a strict simple **downward** crossing.

Once I proved that, a one-crossing theorem followed immediately: excluding the translated branch, \(W\) has at most one zero on a connected overlap interval.

That is one of the cleaner theorem-shaped results of the attack.

Combined with the overlap endpoint data, it means that under 2D closure:
- some overlap subcases have exactly one witness;
- others have zero or one, determined by endpoint signs of \(W\);
- the only genuinely exceptional branch is translated-copy symmetry.

After later corrections, I also found a harder ceiling: pure overlap geometry only forces a witness in the most singular strict overlap subcase. Outside that, 2D closure plus endpoint sign comparison is the right upgraded target.

## 8. The new local fork at a witness

The local witness fork that I think is most useful to hand back is:

At any actual same-value / same-slope witness \(q_*\),
\[
W(q_*)=0,
\]
one has the exact reciprocal-slope tower identities
\[
\Delta^{(m)}(q_*)=\mathcal J_{m,2}(q_*)-\mathcal J_{m,0}(q_*).
\]

So exactly one of the following holds:

1. translated replication:
   \[
   \phi_2(q)-\phi_0(q)\equiv C
   \quad\text{near }q_*;
   \]

2. there is a least even \(N\ge 2\) such that
   \[
   \mathcal J_{N,2}(q_*)-\mathcal J_{N,0}(q_*)\neq 0,
   \]
   and under 2D closure this is forced already at \(N=2\), giving
   \[
   K(q_*)>0.
   \]

So the local obstruction at a witness is not mysterious anymore. It is either exact translated-copy symmetry or an explicit finite even-order transport defect, quadratic under 2D closure.

That is a very strong structural reduction.

## 9. Best no-gos / ceilings worth preserving

These are the sharpest negative results from my lane that are not just restatements of the draft.

Pure overlap geometry does **not** determine witness existence outside the strict sign-forcing overlap subcase. So CR/RC/RR-type witness existence cannot be closed from the window/amplitude data alone.

Translated replication on overlap does **not** survive generically; it forces exact equal-window full translated-copy symmetry of the outer runs. So “translated branch” is really a very rigid exceptional symmetry, not a soft loophole.

Without extra closure or source-side input, the overlap lane does not collapse to a unique witness picture outside the strict sign-forcing case.

There is no reason to expect another local finite-order rescue beyond the current visible transport scalars; the collision-cancellation and generator-audit ceilings support that, and my attack found no good way around them. 

## 10. Best remaining targets from this lane

The next strongest targets now seem to be these.

First, **kill the translated-copy branch**:
\[
R_2=R_0+C,\qquad \widehat Q(u+C)=\widehat Q(u)\text{ on }R_0.
\]
That is now the cleanest exceptional branch on the overlap side. Any RH-specific or package-level reason this cannot happen would remove the main local loophole at once.

Second, **prove the 2D closure law**:
\[
\Xi'(u)=H\!\left(\widehat Q(u),\frac1{\widehat Q'(u)},\Xi(u)\right).
\]
If that lands, the local witness structure becomes rigid immediately, and every nontranslation witness is already quadratic with \(K(q_*)>0\).

Third, outside the strict sign-forcing overlap case, prove the missing **endpoint slope comparison** that forces the sign of \(W\) at the regular overlap end. In CR/RC that is the exact criterion for witness existence.

Fourth, if none of the above lands, then the overlap lane probably really does require package-level or source-side input, not more intrinsic quotient geometry.

## 11. Bottom line

The cleanest full summary of my attack is:

The residual exact fixed-shear obstruction is not plausibly hiding in another local scalar, finite hidden label, or run-local profile invariant. On the overlap side it has compressed to a one-variable inverse-branch transport problem. The concrete scalars are
\[
W(q)=\Delta'(q),
\qquad
K(q)=\Xi(\phi_2(q))-\Xi(\phi_0(q)),
\]
and the reciprocal-slope tower \(\mathcal J_n\).

At any same-value / same-slope witness, the local fork is now explicit:
- either the two outer runs are full translated copies,
- or there is a finite even-order transport mismatch, quadratic under 2D closure.

Translated replication itself globalizes and forces exact equal-window translated-copy symmetry of the outer shells. Outside that exceptional branch, witness existence is **not** determined by overlap geometry alone except in the strict sign-forcing overlap subcase, so extra structure is genuinely needed.

That is the strongest honest recap of the attack and the main structural findings that are not yet fully absorbed into the paper.
